Working long-term EA for GBPUSD H1 in less than 100 lines of code. You can test it, use it, etc. By long term I mean profits are generated in long-term, because EA itself is a day trader.

There is always max one trade active, always sl and tp, EA is active in day hours (at least in Europe, so make sure that you use timezone the same as for example Tickmill broker). Also my algo is very selective, so it's not that there is always active trade or something, but 58% win ration in the last 7 years with tp and sl 50 pips each is enough to make money. It's better than most human traders anyway, but it's not making 100% return in one month... yet.

The attached picture is for high leverage but of course, you can change it. Btw. the graph is showing period since 2011.10.25 to 2018.10.25. Test on 25yo period was positive too, but the slope was not so impressive without modifications (market back then was less violate).

Here is a video of the last year backtest, no bullshit.

It just open position when there is a strong move, that's all. Because there is also ma50 it goes with the trend. If you play with the trend and act when something is happening, then you have statistical advantage over the randomness of the market. Don't try to catch downs and hills, just go with the flow.

It may work with others pairs, but it needs recalibration. Each pair has different range of motion.

A list of the changes I made:

1. Modified the format a bit to make it easier for me to understand the code -- hope you don't mind.

2. Parameterized the following settings: MA periods, lot size, hours, and magic number (taken from @northwind, above)

3. Removed the hard-coded '60' so that it can be used with any time frame

Using MT4 optimizer I found I could improve statistics even further -- e.g. profit factor > 2 and Win Ratio > 60%. Also, using the proper settings, the EA can be used with other pairs and time frames.

For those who are familiar with using MT4's back tester and optimizer I would encourage you to experiment a bit -- you might be pleasantly surprised. And for those who are not familiar with how to back test or optimize, then I encourage you to spend 5 minutes and learn how to.

--- 帖子 #48 ---
This is an interesting EA and it back-tests well -- however, a couple of points to be aware of:

1. The strategy only opens orders. The way that orders eventually get closed is via SL or TP. And this is fine -- however, it means that orders can and will be open for long periods of time. Use the 'visual mode' of MT4's strategy tester and you will see what I mean.

2. The reason why a lot size of '10' is a big mistake is related to point (1) above. Since trades are closed via SL (or TP) that means that first SL will be huge and blow-up the account -- unless you've set the 'Initial Deposit' in the back testing account to $1,000,000. But don't do that -- keep it reasonable, like under $10,000. That is, with an initial deposit of $10,000 and using a lot size of '10' the account will blow-up on the first SL. That is why you should use a smaller lot size -- e.g. 0.1 or 0.01. And that is one of the changes I made in the modified EA I posted earlier.

--- 帖子 #59 ---
Me too -- though, perhaps I can shed some light.

Most brokers's servers are set up for GMT+0 or GMT+2. From Googling I can see that Tickmill (@Pawel's broker) uses GMT+2. The chances are your broker also uses GMT+2 -- so, there is nothing you need to do.

If your broker uses GMT+0 (which is two hours behind GMT+2) then you could increment the 'hour1' and 'hour2' parameters by 2 hours. However, in my hands, these parameters don't make much difference.

The bar data (i.e. OHLC data) arrives from your broker with their server's timestamps. Your local time has nothing to do with it. Your local time only comes into play when manually trading -- e.g. suppose you decide that you favor market conditions when the London banks are open. The UK is currently 6 hours ahead of Central time. So, if you want to trade 8a-2p London time then you'll need to wake up early and trade 2a-8a your time.

When using EAs you don't need to worry about this since most brokers use GMT+2 and your EA doesn't need to sleep.

One last point -- this has to do when trading MANUALLY using the H4 time frame. When trading H4 the GMT+0 and GMT+2 bars arrive at your PC at different local times -- again, GMT+0 is 2 hours behind. This could have a big affect on your trading because GMT+0 bars could be missing some important market events. This is only a problem with H4.

If the PC will go off, then you have to repeat the process, but as long as you keep it going on, everything should be fine.

--- 帖子 #101 ---
It doesn't make any difference how it traded 3 years ago -- you trade in the present (unless you have a time machine).

No EA trades the same over long stretches of time. An EA uses indicators that are simple algebraic formulas with one constant (sometimes more than one). That one constant is optimized for a particular period of time -- e.g. the last 4 months. Since market conditions change, that one constant should also be "refreshed" by re-optimizing the settings (i.e. the indicator constants) from time-to-time.

--- 帖子 #107 ---
Yes -- settings that make a difference should be exposed as input parameters. Some are, some currently are not. But that is like one line of code and slowly, slowly it's getting there.

As far as "self discovery of best param to use" -- wow, that would be a true game-changer for all EAs that have ever been developed or ever will be developed. It's a nice concept, but no one yet knows how to do it -- so, probably won't be implemented in the next version of this EA.

MT4's strategy tester is usually used to determine the best settings for a defined time period. It's easy enough to use -- people who are not already familiar with it should take 5 minutes to learn how to use it.

--- 帖子 #109 ---
Yes -- a portfolio EA that includes many strategies but runs on a single chart. Very familiar with them -- see Forex Strategy Builder -- an excellent product (https://forexsb.com/).

However, in the case of this EA, when you consider it takes MT4's strategy tester only a minute or two to compute the best parameters for a given data horizon (e.g. 4 months) and you only have to do that once every month or two, then that seems like a more realistic (and practical) approach. Unless someone is really, really too lazy and doesn't mind losing money...

--- 帖子 #112 ---
Where did the data for the 100 different market conditions come from? The only market conditions that matter are the current ones, right? Why would someone use 100 market conditions that differed from the current one?

Also, how would one know which of the 100 strategies is the best performer without actually trading all 100?

What does make sense is to trade 100 strategies in a Demo (or micro Real) account and only allow the best performers to trade in your Real account. However, once you let that run for a month or two and then move on to the Real account, the market conditions may have changed again and the best Demo performer may not perform well in the Real account.

Using MT4's Strategy Tester and optimizer, you can determine the best settings for any pair, any time frame. However, this doesn't mean all pairs and time frames will perform well. This is simple and easy to test and something everyone should know how to do, and not expect others to do it for them.

--- 帖子 #113 ---
Quoting ea0setup

--- 帖子 #149 ---
How this EA works...

I hope @Pawel doesn't mind if I point out an interesting feature of his Ultron EA.

For its logic, this EA uses a few moving average calculations -- and that's it. There is nothing magical. However, what I find particularly interesting is how it determines Entry and Exit signals.

Most Expert Advisors use indicators (i.e. algebraic formulas) to look for patterns in the incoming OHLC bar data and generate Entry and Exit signals. When an Entry signal is generated then the EA sends a BUY or SELL order to your broker. When an Exit signal is generated then the EA sends a CLOSE order to your broker. But this EA never sends a CLOSE order!!

So, how does it work? When you open a new position by sending a BUY or SELL order to your broker, the order can also include a Stop Loss (SL) and Take Profit (TP). These are "target prices" the broker may use to close the position. If the EA manages its open positions and explicitly sends CLOSE orders, then the SL and TP are not used.

The Ultron EA does not manage its open positions. After sending a BUY or SELL order it simply lets the trade run -- until the SL or TP target price is hit, at which time the broker closes the position. This is a very clever design on @Pawel's part. For one thing, it greatly simplifies the EA since it doesn't need to implement the logic (and code) for detecting close signals. But more importantly, it also means once a new position is opened you don't need to worry about losing Internet connectivity, or your PC losing power, or Windows Update rebooting your machine, or whatever... Since this EA relies solely on SL and TP to close positions and since these are handled by your broker, then you no longer need the EA (or even MT4, for that matter) -- at least until you are ready to trade again.

Most EAs include logic to detect Exit signals and manage CLOSE orders because it results in better performance. In the case of the Ultron EA, it has a Win Ratio of around 0.55 to 0.60 -- which isn't great, but looks to be good enough.

--- 帖子 #160 ---
I see a lot of comments like that so let me explain why you don't have a single trade for a few days.

I will use this analogy - this EA is not acting like a machine gun. It's more like a sniper rifle. In backtest history, it made something like 450 trades in the last 7 years. That means at average it will open one trade per 3-4 days if you exclude weekend time.

If you are looking for some "exciting" EA, that will shot a trade few times per day, then Ultron is not an EA you are looking for. I believe that trading is built upon patience. This is the biggest principle behind strategy such as this one - you do not trade when the market is not offering exactly what you are looking for. You do not trade when you think you should, you trade when conditions are exactly the way you are looking for. This way you are able to build some statistics and see what works and what do not. If you put your order based on some "woo woo" method, you cannot get any statistical data from your trading record.

Now a quick explanation about "how this simple strategy works".

As many knows, there are 4 moving averages inside the program.

50ma is determining a trend. You do not want to open a long trade when the market is going down.

1ma is only for simplification of the code. I could use bar data for this, but that way it's easier. What does it do? it checks if the current price is not too far from ma50. Why? Because you could get a signal after extremally large movement and usually after such events there is pullback before the market will go that direction again.

And finally, there are 2 moving averages with a period of 9. One for a close price, and one for an open price. They are "real" signals. If they are far enough it means that open and closes at an average are far apart. Why it matters? Because if the price is not too far from ma50 and suddenly there is a big gap between those 2, it means that there is a rapid change in the price. It's combined with a fact that you need 2 bars in the right direction, otherwise, the EA will not open a trade. So EA is looking for a rapid change in the price, but not too big, that is in the direction of a trend.

Now something about tp and sl. Their value is not taken from a wizard. GBPUSD is a very specific currency pair. What it does, it basically jumps from one level to another. And you can clearly see this with this grid that marks round numbers and x.500 numbers. That's why sl and tp are little more than 50 pips. If your "shot" is correct, you have a big chance that it will go a little further than 50 pips. Sl is also about 50 pips because if the trade will hit it, it means that the market went a whole level in another direction. Before it happens there is still a chance that it will go in tp direction. I have attached a screenshot with those levels on a chart. You can see it by yourself.

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

Now, something about "its overfitted because if you change something it performs way worse".

Yeah, because the market is the way it is, not the way we wish it should be. Also, no offence but "you" probably didn't know the details about how it works before this post.

So to make it simple - if you change ma period without changing settings inside the rest of the program, then it's obvious it will not work well. The rest is expecting data from that specific period, if you are changing something with ma's, then you have to change the rest as well because for let's say ma14 the correct distance between open and close is different than for ma9.

The same is for tp and sl. If you are working with GBPUSD, then you are working with the fact that this market respect round numbers a lot.

Also about different pairs: to make this EA work on another currency, you have to change values of ma and values inside the rest of the program, such as distance from ma50, and distances between ma9 open and ma9 close.

If you want to run this on, for example, GBPJPY, you have to change values for different decimal points.

I'm not doing this all, because I'm focused on GBPUSD. When it will be as perfect as can be, I will work on another pair.

For EURUSD you have to take into consideration that it respect also leves 20, 50, 80.

And a final word - I have made some progress, and I have a version that takes even fewer trades but has a smaller drawdown(10%), 1.65 profit factor, and have extremally nice exponential growth. I  think I will post it in a few days when everything will be done. This is a graph from testing on the last 7 years period.

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

And it's not a big deal if an EA open trade not too often. It's better to have a few "snipers" on a chart than one "machine gun" that shoot blindly. I will make more "snipers" such as this one

--- 帖子 #179 ---
I was also thinking about Trailing Stops, but now I think it does NOT make sense for the way this EA is designed.

This EA is designed to run and only close when it hits a SL or TP. In this way it can run for long stretches and overcome small bumps along the way until it reaches its TP.

However, if you add a Trailing Stop -- with the intent to allow it to run even longer -- then I think you have to remove the TP setting. This is because the TP will be hit before you can take advantage of the Trailing Stop.

I think @Pawel has created something special and he explained his philosophy and approach very well in an earlier post. So, now, I'm happy to leave the strategy's design and algorithm to him and just focus to see if Ultron can perform well on other pairs and time frames besides GBPUSD/H1.

--- 帖子 #187 ---
I think it's still okay. What your observation reveals is that it is necessary to "recalibrate" EAs from time-to-time using current data. An EA uses indicators that are simple algebraic formulas -- often with only a single constant (i.e. a MA period). That single constant was computed using historical data. If the historical data no longer matches with current data, then the constant needs to be re-computed.

That isn't to say the EA will always trade the same through all market conditions, it won't. I'm just saying that you can't judge its performance in 2014 unless you calibrate it using data from around that same time.

--- 帖子 #188 ---

--- 帖子 #189 ---
I like that. I do something similar with my other EAs.

However, rather than choosing a specific data horizon, I'll choose a length of time that results in about 100 trades. As an example, for EURUSD/H1 then I'll need around 4000 bars (approximately 8 months) to get around 100 trades -- just to give you an idea. It is important to have a minimum number of trades during the calibration period you've chosen -- otherwise the statistics don't have much meaning.

--- 帖子 #190 ---
There is no correct answer, since it primarily depends on how similar current market conditions are with market conditions when you last calibrated.

Also, it is hard to define what is meant by "similar" market conditions -- that's rather subjective.

If you have lots of EAs and it takes many hours to recalibrate -- then maybe once every few months. But if you only have a few EAs and it takes 10 minutes then I think once a month is fair.

There is also another intangible benefit. When it comes to forex, "data is king". And the longer it takes someone to realize that then the longer will be the struggle. When you take the time to recalibrate an EA, you can't help but pay more attention to the data and notice details you hadn't paid attention to before. And this influences how quickly we learn to improve and refine our approach to trading. When you pay attention to data, it forces you to think.

The reason I mentioned 8 months is because for most of my EAs I need that data horizon in order to reach 100 trades. It might be different for you depending on which pair and time frame you typically trade. My EAs mostly trade EURUSD/H1 and they require about 4000 bars to generate 100 trade signals -- and 4000 H1 bars works out to approximately 8 months.

As with most things in life, it comes down to trade-offs. I could recalibrate over the last 2 days -- but I wouldn't have enough trades for it to be statistically significant. Or, I could recalibrate using 10 years of data -- but then my results would be contaminated with mostly old and stale data. Over time you sort of figure out what fits your trading style and schedule.

And there is nothing magical about 100 trades. I had to pick a number and 100 points is often times considered a minimal sample size for a statistical calculation to have a certain degree of significance.

--- 帖子 #201 ---
What your observation reveals is that it is necessary to "recalibrate" EAs from time-to-time using current data. An EA uses indicators that are simple algebraic formulas -- often with only a single constant (i.e. a MA period). That single constant was computed using historical data. If the historical data no longer matches with current data, then the constant needs to be re-computed.

If you recall from Algebra 101 the algebraic equation for a line is y = mx + b, where 'm' and 'b' are computed from (x,y) data pairs. Different lines have different (x,y) data and, hence, their 'm' and 'b' constants will be different.

The same concept applies to any data source -- if the data source changes then the constants need to be recomputed in order for the algebraic equation to be valid for that data source.

The current settings in the Ultron EA were computed by @Pawel using a data source he described in an earlier post. You are using a different data source -- so, it follows, that the settings used by the algebraic equation(s) in the current Ultron EA aren't suitable for 2008.

As you noted, as the data begins to approach more recent years, then the algebraic equation yields better results.

It is not reasonable to expect such a simple algebraic formula (that uses constants that were computed from a totally different time in history) to perform well for all forex data since the beginning of time.

I think people confuse optimization with AI (artificial intelligence). An EA does not learn. There is no database backing it. It does not get "smarter" by using gobs of historical data. In fact, using too much historical data actually harms the EA because the old data contaminates recent data and the resulting constants (i.e. settings) that are computed may not match well with the most recent data. Since you trade in the present, then that would be considered a bad thing.

I apologize if my tone is somewhat harsh -- it's not personal. Obviously I've discussed / argued this issue before.

By the way -- the differences in the data you noted in your Excel drill-down sound perfectly reasonable -- and the solution is really simple. When you re-calibrate the EA (i.e. re-optimize) then the new settings that get computed will automatically take into account that market conditions have changed. It is not necessary to make any changes to the EA's code or logic -- only the settings.

--- 帖子 #208 ---
Optimization vs Calibration...

I just had an "ah-ha" moment. Maybe it's obvious to most people -- I don't know.

Whenever I see people back test an EA using 2-year old, 5-year old and even 10-year old historical data I can't help but shake my head and wonder why would anyone bother testing an EA using old, stale, irrelevant data. Unless you have a time machine and plan to go back in time to trade, I don't get it.

And then something just occurred to me. I see it written all the time about "optimizing" an EA. MetaQuotes (the developers of MT4) are particularly guilty of this. Plus they perpetuate the use of the word "optimize".

Here are the dictionary's definitions for "optimize" and "calibrate":

optimize: to make as effective, or perfect as possible

calibrate: to determine or check the accuracy of an instrument

When people think they have "optimized" an EA, then it implies a process that was performed once and the EA will then perform well forever more. If you were to instead realize you have simply "calibrated" an EA, then it is understood this is a temporary check and the EA will need to be "re-calibrated" again in the future.

Perhaps because people have this misconception their EA has been "optimized" then it means back tests that date back to 2008 or 2011 or 2015 or even 2017 have relevance to how the EA will trade tomorrow. That is a totally misguided belief. And your own charts and back tests show it -- yet, most everyone chooses to ignore the obvious. Perhaps it's also due to the fact we are all lazy and really wish for it to be true that our "optimized" EA is perfect -- the alternative being we have to spend time to "re-calibrate".

Perhaps if we instead began using the word "calibrate" then it is better understood the current settings are only temporary and will need to be "re-calibrated" in the future (to take into account changing market conditions).

Does this make sense to anyone?

--- 帖子 #211 ---
Hi,

the limit between calibration and curve fitting is very critical and I use this method to avoid flaws. Let me explain what I mean.

If we believe in the logic of the EA, and we believe thet it only needs calibration, it make sense to test it in any year, even in 2014.

If we decide that the period for the calibration is, let's say, 1 month, that's how I tipically do:

at the end of every month (say March to make an example) I run several backtests on the March data and calculate the optimal paramaters; then I becktest the EA on April data and see if I get good results. This way I am sure I am not curve fitting the EA and I replicate the procedure that I would use in real life and in real time.

This is very different from optimizing (or calibrating) the EA on 2018 data and then showing the results for 2018. This is curve fitting and there is no guarantee on the next period results!

I hope to add to the discussion.

Puma

--- 帖子 #212 ---
Curve-fitting is not bad. Curve-fitting is *exactly* what occurs when an algebraic formula is calibrated. In other words -- "curve fitting" is the the more proper algebraic (mathematical) term and is equivalent to what MT4 does when you use it to "calibrate" a strategy. There is no such term as "calibration" in algebra -- rather, we "curve fit" equations. And, believe it or not, we are dealing with algebra.

On the other hand -- there is the problem of OVER curve-fitting. This is what we definitely want to avoid.

If an equity curve is roughly linear over time, then the strategy is probably not OVER curve-fitted. You can tell when a strategy is OVER curve-fitted when you see large steps in the equity curve. Large jumps in an equity curve are due to rare events that are likely never to occur again in the future.

Large steps occur when there is an anomalous, rare event that occurs in your favor. For example, suppose on Tuesday, February 17 there was some news that caused GBPUSD to jump way up. If your settings were to specifically favor February 17 then your strategy would be OVER curve-fitted (because that particular event will probably never occur again on a February 17 in the future).

I hesitate to give "curve fitting" a bad name -- it's a good thing. It is what we do when we "calibrate" a strategy. It is OVER curve fitting that you are trying to avoid.

Your approach to avoid OVER curve-fitting sounds like OOS -- "Out Of Sample" testing -- which is fine, but which many people consider a waste of time. The reason is this -- if the market conditions for April are similar to March then, of course, your settings will continue to work. In other words, if April looks good that doesn't mean your settings are perfect -- it simply means that April's market conditions are the same as March's. Which means nothing -- big deal -- it's sort of what we'd expect.

If you really want to do proper OOS testing then you should take your March 2018 EA and back test it against data from, say, 2015 -- in other words, against market conditions that are almost certainly different than March 2018. If you were to do this then you would find that your EA *always* performed like crap using the 2015 data -- and you might discard the EA thinking it was no good, which would be a shame. So -- it is good that you use recent, 2018 data for back testing and calibration -- but unless you use a completely unrelated data horizon for OOS then it makes no sense, doesn't tell you anything, and is often misleading.

--- 帖子 #215 ---
Hi Robots4me,

I didn't mean to start a discussion on terminology, but just to say that I wouldn't calibrate an EA using the March data, and then test the EA on the same March again. In real life you won't be able to do that!?! What it makes sense is to calibrate parameters using March data and then test what would have happened in the following period (Aprile in this example) equivalent to forward testing.

In your example, "anomalous, rare event" would work also against your EA results but, if you calibrate your EA on the same month you test it, you would exclude as well that event that in reality would deteriorate your real results.... that's why I wouldn't do that... I hope I was clear.

Bye Puma

--- 帖子 #217 ---
I would say that the whole concept of "portfolio" and diversification is dumb. Trading is trading, and it's not the same thing as investing.

Trading is your reaction to the current market. Investing is putting your money for a while into something, that may be beneficial. It seems the same, but it's not. You can invest your money into some stocks, and you can wait a few years and expecting, that if you have chosen the right company, then the value of their stocks will rise.

As a trader, you do not care about "what can happen". You do not try to predict what will happen.

I can show you something. Each of this boxes in the middle is night consolidation on GBPUSD. Not always, but more than 50% times, there will be strong impulse after the price will go outside of this consolidation. You don't care which way it will go, you just act on this knowledge to make money.

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

When you have a portfolio, multiple trades at once, and you are trying to "balance" everything out, then it's not a trading, it's more like a gambling. You do have hope that "you are right". The market does not care about who is right. It's just a statistic that you can use to your advantage.

For example look at poker players. You have champions who are consistently making money, and you have gamblers who act on a "hope" of being right. Being a professional gambler is the same as being a good trader. You do lose, but it's a part of the game. The thing is to earn more than you lose.

And how you can do this? By being good at one thing. I actually don't know almost anything about any other pair than GBPUSD. I do not care about anything else. But this way I can see things that most people do not. This is a reason why I was aware of what do I need to do in order to write Ultron. When I will make Ultron as good as I can, I will write another EA for GBPUSD, because I know some patterns on this pair. There are similarities between let's say EU and GU, but IMO there is no point in trading both of them.

I highly suggest everybody to focus on one thing. I personally don't know any profitable trader who is not focused on 1, maybe 2 currency pair.

And stop trying to predict the future. You don't have to know what will happen. A casino is making money on 100% random events. And it's doing it by having a slight advantage. If you will consistently throwing away 100 euro, and you will earn 101 euro with a 50% chance of each event, you will make money in the long-term run. That whats trading is.

My broker is in the UK, shall I keep the same settings in Hour1 and Hour2 ? I live in the Middle East and my time is GMT+3

--- 帖子 #220 ---
When using an EA it doesn't matter what your local time is -- you could live on the moon.

What is important is your broker's server time. You can figure that out quite easily -- near the upper-left corner of MT4 you'll see "Market Watch: XX:XX:XX". The "XX:XX:XX" is the current time of your broker's server. Using the Internet and some Googling you'll then be able to figure-out if that is GMT+0 or GMT+2 time.

If your broker is using GMT+2, then you do not need to change the default 'hour1' and 'hour2' (since @Pawel's broker's server also uses GMT+2). If your broker is using GMT+0 then you might choose to increment those settings by 2 hours. However, as I mentioned in my earlier post, those settings don't seem to have much effect in my hands, and I have accounts in both GMT+0 and GMT+2.

By the way, the server time may not have anything to do with your broker's location. Again -- your broker could be on the moon. Your broker pays for and receives bid and ask prices from central or commercial banks. This tick data has time stamps associated with each bid and ask price. The time stamp on the tick data is what is important.

--- 帖子 #222 ---
@doha -- if you are GMT+3 and are 1 hour ahead of your broker, then it means your broker's server is GMT+2. I think this is the most common time zone for forex servers.

Absolutely NOT. You keep your computer on 24/7. Your computer may not actually need to be on 24/7, but you really don't want to have to constantly worry about that detail. Or -- you can set up a VPS account for around $10 / month and let that run 24/7.

As I mentioned in my previous response -- this has nothing to do with your local time. The 6:00 and 21:00 refer to the broker's server's time. This is the time stamp associated with the data. If you really, really, really need to conserve on electricity, and if you are using hour1 and hour2 of 6 and 21, then it means you need to keep your computer on between 6 and 21 GMT+2 time. I'll leave it to you to do the conversion of what that means in your local time.

A close signal is by its definition a signal against the trend - assuming that the entry signal was created with a trend respecting strategy.

If you trade with the trend, your only knowledge is that

1. The price will change after some time.

2. There is a greater chance that it will go with the trend not against it.

And the second point means that there is a greater chance of the price going with the trend, but it may go up and down for a while before it will happen. That's why I don't even bother with active position management.

--- 帖子 #241 ---
GMT+0 versus GMT+2

In an earlier post I attempted to answer a question about GMT+0 versus GMT+2. This issue concerns your broker's time and has nothing to do with your local time. The Ultron EA uses 'hour1' and 'hour2' settings -- which refer to GMT+2, since that is what @Pawel's broker uses. @Pawel feels these settings do make a difference and that is why he included them. I use both GMT+0 and GMT+2 brokers, so I decided to pay attention to these settings. If your broker uses GMT+2 then you can continue to use the defaults that @Pawel recommends -- hour1=6, and hour2=21. If your broker uses GMT+0 then you might choose to change them. In my earlier post I said you would need to add 2 hours to convert from GMT+2 to GMT+0 -- but that is wrong. You need to subtract 2 hours. I apologize for the misinformation. Here's a link:
http://www.timebie.com/tz/timediff.p...MT%20+2%20Time

--- 帖子 #242 ---
GMT+0 versus GMT+2 (continued)

Since I use both GMT+0 and GMT+2 brokers then I wanted the EA to automatically do the right thing and adjust the 'hour1' and 'hour2' settings accordingly. That is, I wanted the EA to determine whether the broker is GMT+2 (in which case no change is needed) or GMT+0 (in which case 2 hours should be subtracted).

Below is a code snippet I wrote that seems to work and achieve that goal -- feel free to add it to your *.mq4 code. Or, perhaps @Pawel would consider including something like this in his next version -- I don't know. Or, maybe @Pawel would prefer to keep his Ultron EA simple, lean and mean and not clutter it with non-essential code.

By the way -- the original formatting of the code was easier to read. However, when I add code to a post then, for some reason, ForexFactory automatically reformats it and removes spaces -- probably to conserve space.

##################################################################

// According to @Pawel, Ultron's Hour1 and Hour2 are based on his broker's server using GMT+2,

// so let's honor that.

int iGMTOffset = GMT_GetBrokerOffset();

if (2 == iGMTOffset)

{

// This is the case for GMT+2

// Nothing to do -- same as @Pawel...

}

else

{

// This is the case for GMT+0 and GMT+1

if ((2 - iGMTOffset) > 0)

{

Hour1 -= (2 - iGMTOffset);

Hour2 -= (2 - iGMTOffset);

if (Hour1 < 1)

Hour1 = 1;

}

}

//+------------------------------------------------------------------+

//| |

//+------------------------------------------------------------------+

int GMT_GetBrokerOffset()

{

int AccuracyThresholdInMinutes = 60;

datetime datGMT = TimeGMT();

datetime datBrokerGMT = TimeCurrent();

double dDelta = (double)(datBrokerGMT - datGMT);

dDelta = MathRound(dDelta / (AccuracyThresholdInMinutes * 60));

return ((int)dDelta);

}

@Pawel gives you a gift. The EA works. It reaches the TP threshold and you win!!! -- and, yet, you want more. I would tread carefully when it comes to creating a zillion new versions -- you might discourage the original developer. When the author sees that people aren't appreciative of his winning code and are more interested in squeezing out even more, then he might lose interest altogether. This happens *all* the time on Forex Factory.

It is not true that trailing stops have no effect -- of course they do. It may not be obvious from a single back test chart, but in the code the trailing stop is set prior to the original TP -- otherwise the TP would be hit and the position would close. So, it does change the algorithm and add complexity.

If somebody gives you something that works -- I wouldn't mess with it. If anything, learn how to use MT4's Strategy Tester and optimizer so you can test whether re-calibrating the settings from time-to-time has an effect. But in terms of the code -- I would prefer to keep things simple with only a single "official" version of the EA maintained by the OP. I know that's not possible, because we are all greedy and aren't disciplined enough to know when to push back from the table.

Here's a concept -- learn some minimal MQL coding skills -- then you can experiment to your heart's content...

You did not understand how my trailing stop works! My option can not a priori harm! worst option - this order will be closed by TP But if the price reached TP (68 pips) and went further, then having reached the value of 73 pips, the trailing stop turns on in 2 pips steps - these are the settings in my version of EA, and you don’t need to change them! If the price has not reached 73 pips and has gone back, then the order will close at 68 pips, as programmed in EA. That is, we cannot do worse! Only better. --- 帖子 #320 ---
If you want to open a trade because you think the MAs are close enough, then open a manual trade using the same SL and TP. Since the EA does not manage open orders, then the result will be the same as if the EA had opened the order.

Take a look at the source code -- it is very simple. There are a few conditions that have to be met before a signal is generated -- e.g. x > y. Even if x and y are very, very close -- e.g. x is 4.99999 and y is 5.0, the condition will not be met and a signal will not be generated. If you trade manually the human brain can decide whether close is good enough -- but the EA uses algebra and it doesn't know what "close to each other" means.

--- 帖子 #321 ---
Basically @robots4me described it right. Program does not look for MA that is "close enough". It's a binary situation for a machine - conditions are fulfilled or not.

If I may be honest, I have figured out this EA in maybe 2-3 hours. The same day that I decided to learn mql4. I have tested it a lot, but the process of making this EA work initially was very easy.

Of course, I have many years of experience in the forex market so it's not that anybody can just code this without any knowledge.

Ultron itself is something that is "impossible". Because a lot of people would say "it's impossible to code something simple that make money if it's so simple everybody would be rich by now".

It's a wrong assumption that making money on forex is technically hard. Forex market is not a complicated thing.

What is hard is to not make "human" mistakes. If I would trade Ultron strategy manually, I would lose money probably, because I would overthink this. I would be worried to open a trade, because of "the wrong feel". EA do this without thinking. It's not hard to know what you have to do, the hard part is executing the plan without a second thought.

Of course, for me, personally, it's pointless to spend too much time on developing anything for trading. Why? because I can put maybe 1k USD at maximum into my account and it's simply not worth it. --- 帖子 #364 ---
Personally I wouldn't trust any back test data that is not 99.9%.

You can back test successfully on 90%, and then test again with 99.9%, and you will have vastly different results often times less successful.

Testing on 90% can give some idea of EA operation, but nothing conclusive and anything less than 90% is irrelevant.

--- 帖子 #366 ---
Your stats show a very short data horizon (approximately 2 months) and there are only 14 trades. Statistically this is not significant. Try using a longer data horizon (e.g. about a year) -- you really need about 100 trades for the stats to be meaningful. That's not to say your observation isn't real -- just that they are not statistically meaningful. If your observation is real then it will hold up using a longer data horizon.

For example -- suppose I choose a data horizon where there are 2 trades -- both winners. Does that mean the EA wins 100% of the time? Probably not. But suppose there were 100 trades -- all winners.  In that case it could very well be it wins all the time.  You need a large enough sample size -- e.g. 100 trades -- in order for the results to be statistically significant and taken seriously.  That's the whole purpose of the Tester Report, right?  Statistics (using historical data) is the only way we have to evaluate the potential performance of an EA -- other than actually trading it.

--- 帖子 #369 ---
Actually -- no. You don't have a clue about statistics. This issue has been touched on before -- both here and elsewhere.

Correct -- this is not about whether the EA is good or not but, rather, how one goes about determining the best settings for an EA.

In order to compare two things (your new TP,SL settings versus the default TP,SL settings) you need to take a number of measurements. You took 14 measurements within a specific 2 month period and concluded that TP55, SL68 were better than the defaults for all time periods. That's simply not true. Taking 14 measurements or 5 measurements or 25 measurements during a different period might show the default values work better. Or they might show some other TP,SL combination work better. The data used for your testing will determine which TP, SL combination works best. If you use a different chunk of data, then you will get a different best TP, SL.

For example, using MT4's Strategy Tester and optimizer I found that during that same period of time a different TP,SL combination gave a profit factor of 8.62 and a win percent of 93.3% based on 15 trades. Those are much better than yours. What do you make of that?

This is where statistics and sample size comes in. It tells you whether your testing was sufficient to validate your conclusion. Taking 14 measurements (i.e. 14 trades) within a specific time period (2018.09.16 - 2018.11.14) is not sufficient to conclude the best settings.  It only means that between 2018.09.16 - 2018.11.14 your settings worked better.  It does not mean your settings will work better for other time periods or even in the future.

--- 帖子 #378 ---
Ladies and gentlemen...

With regards to which settings are best -- there are no setting values that work best for all dates. An EA is a simple algebraic formula -- if you don't believe me, just take a look at the *.mq4 source code (it is only a few lines) and see for yourself. Settings that work best will vary depending on the input data (i.e. the test period).

If you intend to trade in the present, then you test with recent data. The one caveat is your test period should include a minimum number of trades (e.g. 100) -- otherwise the results may not be statistically valid.

Built into the MT4 Strategy Tester is an "Optimization" tool. You really must learn how to use it. The "Optimizing" tool can be used to calibrate each setting. In this way you let MT4 compute the best settings for each test period. Forget about all these silly charts -- they are useless content and only serve to fill-up the web page. No one knows what to do with them -- not even the person who posted them.

Finally -- don't over-think this SL, TP issue. You don't understand the market well-enough to make sense of how they are affected by all the interdependent and dynamic variables at play. Very few people understand all the things that are in play -- I certainly don't. If you don't trust @Pawel's default settings, then the best you can do is to let MT4 empirically compute the best values.

--- 帖子 #395 ---
These can be determined empirically. Learn how to use the "Optimization" tool in MT4's Strategy Tester and you will end up with values similar to the defaults you refer to. Though there may be aspects of Forex that are theoretical -- i.e. can be determined with precision in advance -- it is best to think in terms of empirical solutions and probabilities, sort of like gambling, but not exactly.

The settings used by an EA are calibrated using historical data.  Calibrated settings -- whether for a digital instrument or physical one -- are, by nature, determined empirically.

--- 帖子 #396 ---
Thanks for the reply

--- 帖子 #397 ---
I agree. And I'd like to point out something about Equity curves. You'll notice the X-axis is NOT time but, rather # trades. When your eyes see an Equity curve that appears linear then you assume it grows gradually and consistently over time. But that is not necessarily the case. It could be that all those trades took place 7 years ago and then nothing for the past 6 years. Or, it could be that trades occur in clusters with long gaps in between. You have to look at the time stamps of the actual trades in order to get an accurate picture whether an EA performs smoothly or sporadically over time.

--- 帖子 #430 ---
Yes -- I also like to check for that. However, it depends on how you determine the main trend. If you ask 10 traders you'll get 11 different responses.

The Ultron EA uses a slow 50 MA. This can serve a couple of purposes: (a) as a "proxy" support / resistance, and (b) main trend indicator.

In the Ultron code a SELL signal can only be generated if the other MAs are below the slow 50 MA, and a BUY signal can only be generated if the other MAs are above the slow 50 MA. I compared it with the Ichimoku Kumo Cloud indicator and the 50 MA tracks closely with the Kumo Cloud. So -- though the slow 50 MA may not be the most sophisticated way to monitor the main trend, it's probably good enough. And many other EAs use something similar.

This is good stuff -- you're not off topic.

I see what you mean by the LTF (Long Time Frame) indicator -- but for me that is much too long. Most of my trades last only a few hours, so a D1 trend that is 24x longer than my H1 EA just doesn't work for me. Using a D1 time frame it looks like for the next month all trades would have to be SELLs. If you were to suggest an H4 trend monitor that could be more reasonable -- but I still wouldn't use it. The built-in 50 MA serves as your LTF trend monitor. I think anything more would hurt more than it helps.

It's easy enough to test, though -- simply change the 50 MA to a 1200 MA (i.e. 24 x 50) and run a back test in MT4's Strategy Tester. See how many trade signals are generated during the course of a year.

Here we go. Monitor 28 pairs at a glance. Push and email notification, sound and pop alert.

Have never been able to set up email function therefore could not test this alert. If some one has actually set up a working email in MT4, please provide specific instructions and the name of the email provider that worked.

Have provided two templates, one with alert set to true and one with alert set to false. As a change of forex pair triggers the alerts, you should use the chart with alert set to false to review different pairs.

There are three levels of signals. Level 3 when the signal has just appeared, level 2 when the signal is up to two bars old and level 1 when the signal is 4/5 bars old.  You can set the desired colors through the parameters. When alerts are set to true, alerts will be issued for all the three levels without distinction.

The pair icon can be viewed in a separate window through the relevant parameter.

For a four digit broker, set the parameter "FiveDigitMultiplier to 1. For a five digit broker, it should be 10.

--- 帖子 #478 ---
Just to be clear to everyone -- the Ultron EA has NOT been gaining money the past few months. That is extremely bad misinformation. The Ultron EA was published at the end of October. There have been a few real trades since then -- one winner and a couple of losers.

What people have been doing is playing around with MT4's Strategy Tester and extrapolating the results into the future. That is called "wishful thinking" -- and, not, "gaining money".

MT4's Strategy Tester is primarily used to work out the bugs when developing an EA or indicator. It is notoriously bad at predicting the future.

Ultron is very simple and looks promising. But no one should spread rumors that it has a history of gaining money until it really does have a history of gaining money.

As for GBPUSD fluctuating -- yes, obviously. However, in forex "fluctuating" is GOOD -- that is how you make pips. If it didn't fluctuate and was flat then there would be no opportunities to trade. Remember -- forex is different than stocks and bonds since we don't buy and hold with the expectation it will go up over time. In forex traders don't care if a currency pair goes up or down -- it's all the same to us.

--- 帖子 #548 ---
I've been backtesting the ULTRON-3.4_Exponential_MM_TR EA fairly extensively and, as everyone else here has shown, it generates a pretty good profit when configured correctly. I do, however, think the trailing-stop system is flawed. It doesn't make sense to me to move the stop to where the original TP was only after the price has hit the TP. Is it possible to add a more traditional (and actual) trailing stop to this? I.e., a stop that either moves in steps based profit pips, or a trailing stop where you define a set gap between SL and where the price is?

I understand how some people feel having a trailing stop can actual decrease profits, but I'm interested in this feature simply for testing. I feel, on the contrary, that orders without a set TP but with a good trailing-stop system could actually perform even better, again with good configuration. Now I don't know how code any of this in MT4 myself otherwise I would, but clearly there's some clever people here who can probably add such a feature, hence this post.

What do you guys think, can it be done?

--- 帖子 #559 ---
GU is in flat with 15/11 about today. During this time , the EA has at least twice reached an equity of about +300 pip, but since TP was more than 600 pip, it has not fixed this profit. Accordingly, in the negative balance twice triggered SL and fixed a loss of about -500 pips.

The task is: to reduce losses of the adviser in the flat. To solve this problem, I suggest still add him a trailing stop in the form of a dynamic stop loss SL, which is set in the settings as % of the profit and moves the EA as the profit increases with a given step H. A similar idea was expressed in :

_https://www.mql5.com/ru/forum/291798

the EA operation would look like this:

- if the price goes to minus, the usual fixed SL stop loss is triggered (as it is already set in Ultron).

- if the price moves in plus, starts to work new trailing stop, which is different in that the growth of profits in the open position, SL grows in increments of H but as a percentage of the profitable points.

Then in ULTRONE settings should be 2 SL: SL- and SL+

For example:

Setting: Stop loss (SL+) = 50%

Position profit is 100 pips - > so move Stop loss at a distance of 50 pips from the current price (fixed 50 pips profit).

Position profit is 180 pips - > so move Stop loss at a distance of 90 pips from the current price (fixed 90 pips profit).

Position profit is 200 pips - > so move Stop loss at a distance of 100 pips from the current price (fixed 100 pips profit).

Setting: the Stop loss (SL+) = 25%

Position profit is 100 pips - > so move Stop loss at a distance of 25 pips from the current price (fixed 75 pips profit).

Position profit is 180 pips - > so move Stop loss at a distance of 45 pips from the current price (fixed 135 pips profit).

Position profit is 200 pips - > so move Stop loss at a distance of 50 pips from the current price (fixed 150 pips profit).

And the parameters SL+ : the beginning of operation and the step H, the author could calculate at the levels that he found for GU.

If you like the proposal, the programmers will find on this link above, on page 2, the EA codes with such an algorithm as stop loss in % of profit.

Good luck to everyone

--- 帖子 #564 ---
Hi. What is the GMT time zone where your MT4 operates?

--- 帖子 #565 ---
Your local time zone -- that is, the time zone of your MT4 session -- is irrelevant. You could be on the moon. The time zone of your broker's server is what is most important since it is the one that sends tick data. Each tick has a time stamp and the Ultron EA makes decisions based on that time stamp (and NOT on your local time). MT4 displays the time of your broker's server in the upper-left corner, and you can then figure out which GMT time zone it operates in. Please do not ask here how to figure it out -- you have Internet and Google and should be able to do it yourself. Or, you could contact your broker and simply ask them -- but then they would know you really don't have a clue how retail forex trading and MT4 works.

--- 帖子 #602 ---
[quote=salimc;11976863]
Hi salimc. Ultron will open a trade during the London session of the trading day, which is the best time of the day to trade due to the high volume. However, keep in mind that it is purposefully not designed to trade everyday necessarily. Ultron will open a trade only if the moving averages/momentum, etc... gets triggered. This is what makes this a good system that Pawel designed. I personally don't trade every day either. I tend to open manual trades when I see the market hits a certain level of support or resistance. Over the years, I learned that being patient is key to making any dent in the forex markets.

Pawel initially designed Ultron to work primarily on the GBP/USD (The Cable).

--- 帖子 #627 ---
I started reading back through older posts and just realized how insightful this is. I used to go nuts trading every pair then realized it wasn't doing me any good and instead began to focus exclusively on the GBP/USD pair. I always hear "But there's more opportunities and money on other pairs!" - Yeah, and more risk and loss too. Settling on one pair has been the most effective decision I've ever made in Forex trading.

--- 帖子 #628 ---
That's not about more risk and loss or more opportunities and money that's about diversification. You can settle on one unique asset: forex. Then you can settle on one unique pair: cable. Then you can settle on one unique time window: 7-20. Then you can settle on one unique market condition: volatility. The you can settle on one unique strategy: using MA. Then you can settle on one unique parameter: 0.00024. etc.

That's the definition of overfitting.

Basically GU is EU-EG (example). Anything working on GU should work on EU and EG.

By the way, IMO, +-200 trades is not statistically significant.

--- 帖子 #792 ---
if profitTrailing = true, then TP does not work. Works SL and tral. Profit is fixed only trailing stop
if profitTrailing = false, then TP and SL work without trailing stop

in the version of ULTRON 3.2.0 VTB tral is activated at a distance of 5p. above TP level.
If the price goes further to plus, tral moves in steps 2p.
If the price turns around, the profit will be fixed at the level of TP, which is set in the settings (68p.)

--- 帖子 #853 ---

--- 帖子 #854 ---
It dictates the risk in lot size. So for example, if you have a $10,000 and set the RR to it's default of 10, it will start trading lots of 0.5 and scale the lot size per order to maintain the same RR. This is relatively low-risk given the account size versus the lot size you're trading. If you set the RR to 25 let's say on that same $10,000 account, it will begin with trading lot sizes of 1.25, which is considered higher risk. It essentially defines the starting lot sizes, and then maintains that ratio of lot-size to account balance for all future trades. That is, at least, how I understand it.

--- 帖子 #885 ---
So what happened to me, just for the sake of information, is that my time settings were set to 6 and 23 (for whatever reason). This caused a buy order to open around 4pm EST yesterday. But in back-testing, with the time settings set correctly to 6 and 21 (my broker time is GMT), that buy order doesn't trigger. Case and point: Make sure your time settings are scaled correctly from your brokers GMT because it does effect when and where the EA opens moves. If your broker is GMT+2, then use 8 and 23, if GMT-4 then use 2 and 17, etc.

A lot of them list whether or not they change for DST. For anything GMT+2 or EST, it changes to GMT+3 starting tomorrow. And then you have to change the values of the EA accordingly (default is for GMT which is 6 and 21). NOTE: GMT servers stays the same all year and are not affected by DST.

More info on time-changes in Forex:

https://newportquant.com/time-zone-d...er-time-part2/

The last move the EA made was on March 7th. It hasn't opened anything since. It usually only opens 1-2 positions max a week. OK, here's my version of Pawel's EA: ULTRON_PDV_1.

Modifications:Parameterised all hard-coded values to allow further customisation/optimisation. Amended to work with other currency pairs and timeframes (not just GBPUSD H1). Corrected the time filter. Corrected SL and TP settings to take spread into account. Changed order submission to comply with ECN broker rules. Converted all SL/TP/Slippage to pips and catered for all price feeds. Added money management option as well as fixed lots. Added a trailing stop function. Added news filter (requires indicator FFCal - see attached) Added info panel. Parameters:
Attached Image (click to enlarge)

The defaults are the best settings I've found so far (see back test report below), but please feel free to test and post any seetings that you find are better.

The time filter defaults are in GMT, so you will need to adjust them according to your broker's GMT offset and DST.

Back test report:

The default hours for my version of the EA are 07-19 GMT, so with the broker offset of GMT+2 plus DST, you will need to set the time filter to 10-22.

--- 帖子 #989 ---
Hi,

FFCal isn't required if you have NewsFilter set to false.

If you want to turn the news filter on, you need to place FFCal.mq4 in the Indicators folder in MT4. It should all then work as intended, however, it does rely on the news calendar being available from ForexFactory, and sometimes that screws up and you can get false positives (i.e. it thinks it's news time all the time!).

Regarding the trend, this needs to be improved, but currently it's simply looking at the MAs and using the entry logic to determine whether it should be looking for longs or shorts.  As I say, this needs to be improved, and I'll work on it for the next version.

Some food for discussion: In the period starting from 2015 there have been lesser results, as has been mentioned. The typical consecutive wins/losses however make it possible to use some form of a betting sequence like inverse d'Alembert or 1-3-2-6. After performing some in depth calculations I found this:

The blue line is the standard exponential increase (1.1/0.9), the others are different betting sequences on top of that. The numbers are net gain, start capital 10000, starting with 1 lot, original SL/TP, no trailing!

Enhancements:Added option to completely hide the info panel (speeds up testing). TP can now be zero...order will only close when price hits (trailing) SL or retracement. Added Retrace Exit feature. --- 帖子 #1058 ---
I've never heard of this, although what you're describing sounds very reminiscent of the Roulette Trader Money Management strategy: start with a multiplication factor of 1, if the trade wins, increase the factor by 1. Use a set maximum factor and reset back to 1 when either the target is reached (thus 'locking in' the profit already achieved) or a loss is incurred.

Is this along the lines that you're thinking of? If so, then I've already coded an EA that does this and wouldn't take much to integrate with Ultron.

--- 帖子 #1064 ---
Similar, but not quite the same. The sequence 1-3-2-6 for ex. cannot be done with a fixed factor. You would need to specify your preferred sequence as (x,x,x,x,...), can be 2, 3 or more numbers. For the Ultron we don't need more than 4 I think.

Example: start lot =1, and changes during a winning streak to 3,2, and 6 lots. This repeats until you lose where it gets reset to 1 lot (or better to a risk related value).You would then need an input for the base lot (1) and another one for the sequence (3,2,6) in this case.

If you already have similar code you might give it a go!

--- 帖子 #1067 ---
This has been on my mind for some time too.

I'm considering allowing different forms of trailing stop, such as:None Regular (starts trailing when x pips in profit) Immediate (starts trailing as soon as the price is x pips ahead of the SL, and then by a certain step) EMA (SL follows the curve of a specified EMA, trailing x candles behind). Factored (starts trailing immediately the order in opened, and trails according to the % that the price has moved toward the TP) In the last scenario, for example, if the TP and SL are both 100, the SL is moved 2 pips for every 1 pip the price moves (because the ratio between the SL and TP is twice that of the Open Price and TP).  I'm thinking that perhaps this should be geared down by a % factor to avoid closing too tight too soon, e.g. 80%, so the SL will move 16 pips for every 10 that the price moves?

Thoughts?

--- 帖子 #1068 ---
As soon we reduce the SL, the probability of hitting the target also gets smaller so I was thinking in the line of only taking a part (or max 100%) of the favourable excursion. So, price moves 20 pips+, SL is reduced with 10 pips or so (50%  of the gained pips).  I looked through some 100 trades and this gives a good result.

--- 帖子 #1134 ---
In LITE_3 there is no risk percent, I have already explained this, it uses a different system for calculating the initial lot, even in the settings it is called Risk Ratio
for example:
balance 3000, RR 10 - the initial lot will be 0.90,
balance 1000 , RR 10 - the initial lot will be 0.30 and so on)
but these values may differ slightly there is a dependency on account leverage

(AccountBalance() * AccountLeverage() * risk_percent * 0.01)

--- 帖子 #1154 ---
I've just checked, and Forex.com appear to have a server time of GMT-12 (https://www.myfxbook.com/forex-broker/forex-com/10).

The EA checks the trading hours set against the current broker's time. So when our orders opened at 17:00 GMT, your broker's server time would have been 05:00, which would explain why it didn't open an order.

I would recommend double-checking your broker's offset and using the new Broker Server Offset parameter to obtain the correct time window. e.g. if your broker offset really is -12, then set the start and end hours to the default of 07 and 19, and then enter -12 for the broker offset and you should be good to go.

EDIT: I've made a small change to display the current server time on the info panel.  Hopefully this should make things a little clearer for users.  I'll upload the change over the weekend.

--- 帖子 #1166 ---
Actually, I may owe you an apology - the myfxbook page I linked to may not be accurate, and I think it's worth you contacting your broker to make sure.

Now for the apology...I think there may be something wrong with the time filter code!

I copied Pawel's original code to begin with, and amended the calculation used, but I didn't think to check the MQL4 functions used.  The time filter uses the function "Hour()" to check the trading times, but the MQL4 documentation says that this is the last known server time "when the program starts and is not updated while the program is running".

If this is correct, then it is a lottery as to WHEN you start the EA, as that will be the hour that the program thinks it is...all the time!  So, if you start the EA out of trading hours, it will always be out of trading hours!

The problem with this is that this doesn't work this way in the strategy tester, so for a developer who doesn't know this, the EA LOOKS like it's working when tested but when run for real, it doesn't.

I've amended the time filter to use the correct functions "TimeHour(TimeCurrent())", which IS updated on every call, and will post the new version later today.

--- 帖子 #1169 ---
I've coded hidden SL and TP before and they are a right pain in the arse to do, especially with multiple orders and moving stops.  The only real reason to use them is if you don't trust your broker and think they may be stop hunting...in which case, you are better off finding a broker you DO trust.

To be honest, your comment raises several things in my mind that I think are worth pointing out:You shouldn't keep that amount of money in your trading account:Black Swan events do happen, and they can wipe out your entire account! Brokers can go bust, and they will take your funds down with them. Regulation only protects about the first 20k - anything more than that will be lost.  You should be using a true ECN broker:The broker makes its money solely from commissions and swaps and does NOT make money when you lose, so there's no conflict of interest.  The test results are not accurate once you get to that size, because orders of that size may not get filled, either on open or on closure, due to lack of liquidity.If you use a broker that "guarantees" your orders will be filled, I can assure you that they are crooks: they take the other side of your order (basically they are betting AGAINST you), and make money when you lose, and lose money when you win!
They have a vested interest in making sure you lose!

These brokers are NOT ECN brokers, and most likely are not regulated.  So if your current broker "guarantees" your orders will be filled, you need to change brokers NOW.  When your account gets to being several hundred thousand in size (if you get that lucky!) then you should employ an 80/20 rule: pull out 80% of your capital and save it in a non-broker account, and then gear your EA to trade the remaining 20% as though it was the 100%.  You will  probably need high leverage for this though, and may have to play around with the percentages to make this work (maybe 50/50 will be enough for you).  But the idea is that you protect your main capital, and if your trading account does suffer a wipeout, you still have capital to start again.

Of course, the choice is yours, but this is what I aim to be doing.

If you're wondering about what good broker to use, then, if you're not in the USA, I can thoroughly recommend my broker IC Markets.  They are regulated, true ECN leverage of up to 500:1, and have some of the smallest spreads around.  I've been with them for well over a year and have had no problems with withdrawing funds.  Check them out.

--- 帖子 #1173 ---
as for hiding SL and TP - I came across this and will share observations: The plus is that the broker does not see SL and TP, but there is also a minus: standard, open SL and TP are processed directly by the broker, if the broker is good, then it works quickly. If SL and TP are hidden, then in this case the signal is already processed by the program and in any case it takes more time, which means that the accuracy of the triggering of such a device will decrease. And your SL will not work 70 pips, and maybe 80, or even worse, and it may not work at all. And then the result of trading will not be at all what you expect)

I certainly gave a tough example, but it can be.

--- 帖子 #1178 ---
Risk percentage of 10 on a €99,500 account means that you're risking 10% of your entire account (€9950) on a single trade.  Assuming you're using the default of 70 pips, this means a lot size of 16.09 lots (this will vary depending on the EURUSD price, so may have worked out at 16.31 at the time).

Your broker will then apply margin to this, and if the margin requirement is too high, the order is rejected.  My assumption from this is that you're using a low leverage account - maybe 50:1?  Is that correct?

--- 帖子 #1195 ---
ULTRON_PDV_104

Updates:Added 'Full leverage' as a money management option. Added 'Progressive factors' as a lot multiplier. Full Leverage

This money management option determines lot sizes as a percentage of the full leverage available for the instrument for your broker.  Essentially this works the same way as Feex's calculation in Lite3.  This can be risky if there is a long run of losers, but can recover quite quickly when there's a long run of winners.

Progressive Factors

This is an implementation of the progressive betting strategy that takes advantage of strings of wins to boost profits, while attempting to minimise the effect of strings of losses.

Basically each lot (whether fixed or dynamic) is multiplied by the next in a series of factors, which the cyle repeating.  When a loss in encountered, the sequence is reset to start at the first factor again.

The default uses factors (multipliers) of 1,3,2,6 expressed as a comma-separated list of percentages (100,300,200,600).  These can be amended to whatever values you wish, and there is no limit to the number of factors you use.

To scale down the factors you simply reduce the numbers (e.g. 100,130,120,160 equates to multipliers of 1,1.3,1.2,1.6).

You cannot use both of these features at the same time as you will incur a margin call very quickly.

You cannot use Progressive Factors with MaxTrades > 1.

Hiya,

Although the news filter works (i.e. it stops trading and then restarts afterwards) I haven't actually tested the effects of having it on.

As you can't test the news filter historically, the closest I would be able to get would be to run the EA with it off, and then go through the trades and attempt to match them to the high impact news and speeches to see if they would have been avoided.  I haven't done this yet, but may do.

Generally speaking though, with other EAs, I would cease trading at least an hour before major news, and restart after about an hour afterwards.  However, as we're working on a H1 timeframe, I  suspect that the news filter will probably have little impact, but please feel free to try it out on demo.

--- 帖子 #1267 ---
To add to this I've been doing all kinds of tests and optimizations over the weekend and so far these are the best settings I've found with a good profit and acceptable DD. Yes there were more profitable settings (+$100k) but the DD was over 50% which is past my threshold.

SL: 100

TP: 0

Progressive: True

Risk %: 4

Risk Basis: Full leverage

Tr Stop: 40

Tr Step: 2

With these settings tested over the last year, results from $1k start is $60k profit with 3.56 PF and 43% DD.

Setting Risk % to 5 would raise the profits to over $144k, but the DD goes up to 52% which is personally too high for live trading.

I believe it is better to use a break even stop with trailling steps.

Example initial TP: 100 pips, SL: 50 pips

In case trade is in 20 pips profit, trade will protected to get not in negativ with break even 20, step 4 pips -> SL ist now at entry point.

If you use trailling stop at 20 pips with 4 pips step. The trade will have SL 30 pips below entry point.

--- 帖子 #1329 ---
Ignore your personal GMT offset, it's just your broker's server offset we're interested in.

In your case, you should leave the start and end hours as 07 and 19, and set the broker offset to 3.  That should make the EA trade the correct times.

The only thing you may want to adjust is when Daylight Saving Time is updated:
During winter, your broker offset would normally be +2, and this is what you should normally enter in the parameters.In the spring, when your broker moves to DST, you add 1 to the offset (so, now it will be +3).When the UK moves to DST a few weeks later, you need to drop 1 from the offset (because the London session has moved forward an hour), so +2.In the autumn, when your broker comes off of DST, you need to take 1 away again, leaving the offset on +1.When the UK then comes off of DST a few weeks later, you need to add 1 back on , so the offset is, again +2 for the winter.

A bit convoluted, I know, but you only have to amend the offset which saves trying to calculate the base hours all the time.

Hope this helps.

--- 帖子 #1332 ---
[quote = PaulDV; 12130923] {quote}忽略你的个人GMT抵消，这只是我们感兴趣的经纪人服务器抵消。在你的情况下，你应该把开始和结束时间保留为07和19，并设置经纪人抵消这应该使EA交易正确。您可能想要调整的唯一事项是更新夏令时：在冬季，您的经纪人偏移通常为+2，这是您通常应在参数中输入的内容。在春天，当您的经纪人移动到DST时，您将偏移量加1（因此，现在它将是+3）。几周后，当英国转移到夏令时，你需要从抵消中减少1（因为伦敦会议已向前移动一小时），所以+2。在秋季，当您的经纪人退出DST时，您需要再次取消1，将偏移量保留为+1。几周之后，当英国从夏令时退出时，你需要重新加上1，所以偏移量是冬天的+2。我知道，有点令人费解，但你只需要修改偏移量，这样可以节省尝试计算基准时间的所有时间。希望这会有所帮助。[/ quote]

Your explanation makes me very happy.

--- 帖子 #1340 ---
Yeah, unfortunately it's just bad timing I think.  During back testing there have been a number of consecutive losses, so it can and will happen.

Regarding the trailing stop; it's a personal preference of course, hence why it's parameterised, but in my experience, holding out for the bigger wins can often be counter-productive over time, and often it's more profitable long-term to go for the smaller quick wins.  For me, at least, I prefer the smoother equity curve of smaller wins over the heart-wrenching wild swings in profit you can get when going for "the big one".

--- 帖子 #1341 ---

--- 帖子 #1349 ---
I wouldn't get too hung up on backtests. I appreciate they offer some kind of indication of performance, but personally I would be analysing my results constantly throughout the year and optimising/adjusting settings depending on market conditions. i.e. we may start minimising the SL or TS depending on ADR changes. Summer months are usually worse for trading and have lower volatility, so I may even stop trading full stop or look at reducing my target profits. These sort of things backtesting doesn't take into account. We know that the EA works, so now it's a case of 'forward' testing it with multiple variables which I think this thread is doing well!

--- 帖子 #1385 ---
But my step was 2, so doesn't that mean after 40 pips in the green the trailing stop increases every 2 pips? I.e. 40, 42, 44,46 etc ?

--- 帖子 #1386 ---
No, that's not how trailing stops work.  The TSL is how big of a gap you're happy to have once the SL starts to trail, the Step is how many pips to move the stop when the price gets ahead of the stop by the TSL.

If you use 40/2, every time the price is 40 pips or more from the TSL, the TSL is moved to 38 pips behind the price (locking in 2 pips).

If you use 45/13, when the price is 45 pips or more ahead of the TSL, the TSL is moved to be 32 pips behind the price (locking in 13 pips).

Hope this helps.

--- 帖子 #1437 ---
Attached Image (click to enlarge)

OK in all testing in last 1 year, we have picked up huge drawdown- according to some it is scary. 84% - Relative Drawdown.

And this has happened during May first 14 days. It is high volatile quick swings, which has affected these trades. This is the only 1 single instance in whole year where there were 4 consecutive losses.

Picture outlines which are those losing trades & how many pips was it before the market went in making the trade breakeven.

From looking at it,

What about this idea-

1. Bringing Spread into trade open. On a volatile market - spread is usually high.

2. If a trade which is opened goes into negative say about 60% or 70% of the original SL, then TP should be moved to Breakeven.

example, if setting SL is 100 pips, and trade goes into negative about 70 pips, our original TP should now be set to Break even price, so that when it retraces, order gets closed.  If the price comes into a break even range - say 10-15 pips range. new SL should be break even range.

new TP will be same or closer to our initial open price. And new SL should be 10-15 pips range of the new TP. That way, even if the price rebounds back into negative, we only take 10 pips loss.

I know some trades would close with this strategy, but i think, if this is coded, we might reduce drawdown, and we already have good winners.

What do you & @PaulDV say about this.

- For me changing ma-gap from 50 to 56 doesnt change much in terms of drawdown. main issue in previous was relative drawdown. profit was more than happy on both.

--- 帖子 #1438 ---
On this backtesting with Open prices is not a good idea, it would show anything.

Order opening depends on Volume, so it not at the open price. full ticks need to be available to get proper testing.

And even with lot of testings, it only gives us high confidence on how an EA performs on historical data. It is probability only and not 100% guaranteed results. So still risk is at large. you still take general trade precautions, such as closing orders during weekend, and closing EA during NFP & other major news events. It usually helps performance of EA better.

--- 帖子 #1458 ---
ULTRON_PDV_105

Updates:Startup messages are now output to the log. Improved some startup check messages. Improved the efficiency of the info panel. Added trade statistics to info panel. Detect the cycle on startup if using progressive lot sizes. Allow for starting cycle at a specific point. Amended the logic for the retrace feature to improve profitability. If you leave the broker offset as zero, you are now prompted when starting the EA to ensure that you mean to do this, as most brokers are not on GMT time.

The Retrace Exit feature is now on by default, and you specify the percentage of the stop loss you are prepared to allow the price to retrace before triggering the retrace exit.  Once triggered, the TP is moved to the 50MA, and the trade will either hit the SL (for a full loss) or the TP (for a partial loss).

This update improves the profitability and drawdown as shown below:
Attached Image (click to enlarge)

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

As you can see, the profitability is increased slightly, and the average loss is greatly reduced, resulting in a lower drawdown.

--- 帖子 #1472 ---
But you are free to use non fitted version, according to you. Every version 104 or 105 all do have on and off features, You can switch off all features and just use TP & SL.

Let me say, why it is not curve fitting.

Back testing & Machine Learning based on historical data and improving the model is just about training your EA on old data to simulate forward movement. thats what EAs are for.

All March forward trades were repeated on back test as well on tick data.

Now coming to back testing or even for that matter EA, there is no guarantee, it is all about probability only. Markets are nothing but behavior of people trading against various factors- whether it is news, other economic factors or just speculation.

And every strategy is just a pattern which is observed and we try and fit. a repeat of the pattern and see whether it is successful.

Here on this EA, first we got the good signal, which allowed us to have more winners than losers - higher probability.

Then we focused on maximising our % of winners by bringing in Trailing Stop effectively managing it - again flexibility allowed.

Lot size calculation to allow for different styles to see how we maximise our winners.

To reduce drawdown, we saying, lets minimise our loss by reducing losers, even if it sacrifices few of our winners- thats where new feature came in. I think it did reduce a bit. not too much but a bit of drawdown. - if a trade goes almost 80%, then it is better to close it when it retraces, not expecting it to become a winner. already it has made a move of about 50pips or something. we saying, it is retraces to Moving Average 50, which is one of MA we using on this. It would be a good point to close it with that loss. it is just a pattern which has been observed to reduce losers.

We only have 1 incident of consecutive losing trades according to our signal. we can always ignore it and move on.

if you can, please help us find a reason why the signal formula worked better since August 2018 better. what made it good only now. how long will this run last.

Hi Fareed,

I've performed some analysis on the results for the past two years, looking at wins/losses on a day of the week basis, and the trades appear to be fairly evenly distributed across the week, with the exception of Tuesdays, which has nearly double the trades of any other day.  Losses are also fairly evenly distributed, with Friday trades being no different to trades opened on any other day of the week.

Of course, that's historical, and running on forward testing could produce completely different results...
