--- 帖子 #1578 ---
Hit SL 70.

--- 帖子 #1579 ---
Yes, this is the Retrace Exit feature.  When the price retraces 83% of the SL, the EA basically decides that the trade is a loser, and moves the TP to the 50MA.  The idea is that if the price then reverses a little it will stop out for a smaller loss than a complete loss.

In this instance, it didn't make any difference though, as the trade finally hit the SL anyway.

--- 帖子 #1587 ---
thanks,,,got it

sometimes DD goes very high.....it should maintain entry point in base of weekly support and resistance.....u can try davit fibo indicator code.....best one for entry
Inserted Code double wclose= iClose(Symbol(),PERIOD_W1,1);
double wopen = iClose(Symbol(),PERIOD_W1,1);
double whigh = iHigh(Symbol(),PERIOD_W1,1);
double wlow=iLow(Symbol(),PERIOD_W1,1);

double calPivot = (whigh+wlow+wclose)/3;

double calRange=(whigh-wlow);

// ***** for resistance *********************************************

double R38  = calRange*0.382+calPivot;
double R61  = calRange*0.618+calPivot;
double R50  = calRange*0.50+calPivot;
double R78  = calRange*0.786+calPivot;

// ***** for support *********************************************

double S38  = calPivot-calRange*0.382;
double S61  = calPivot-calRange*0.618;
double S50  = calPivot-calRange*0.50;
double S78  = calPivot-calRange*0.786;

entry should not exceed R61 and S61 in each direction

Attached File(s)   Davits Pivot V3.2 Auto.mq4

25 KB
|
409 downloads

Myself I've put up a few high volatile pairs such as EURAUD, EURNZD, GBPNZD, GBPAUD, GBPCAD etc for forward testing on demo and they are showing promise. In time I'll post my results. This pairs make a lot of pips in short moves/distances and when they begin to move they tend to really move with not much pullbacks. But you don't want to be caught on the wrong side . If my results prove any good then we'd need to inculcate the partial closeout feature in Ultron so as to avoid closing out trades too early due to short pullbacks that usually take out the retrace feature.

--- 帖子 #1624 ---
No worries.

In the Strategy Tester, you will see a button that says "Tick data settings".  Click on this and it will bring up TDS.  At the bottom, there should be two dropdowns: one for GMT Offset, the other for DST.  Set GMT Offset to zero and DST to none.

There should also be a checkbox for "Use variable spread".  Check this.  Then click OK.

The Strategy Tester should then update the HST files (the tick data) to be at the raw GMT times.  Now, when you run the EA, the Start and End Hours will be GMT, and you can set Broker Offset to zero.

Your tests will now all be at GMT.  When you run for real (on either a demo or live) you can leave the Start and End hours at the optimum settings you've found, and simply set your broker's offset and you should get the same results going forward.

--- 帖子 #1633 ---
That doesn't do what you think it does, and is virtually useless for coding EAs.

It returns the time in GMT using the LOCAL PC's GMT offset, and doesn't give you the GMT time based on the server's offset.  This is why you will see many EAs asking for your broker's offset.  Those that don't usually assume that you have entered the times adjusted to the server's time.

--- 帖子 #1662 ---
Thanks - that's much easier for my brain!

OK, so there seems to be a slight difference between this and what @majamivice is asking for.

You're saying don't lock in until we reach TSL start + LockInProfit; @majamivice is saying lock in when we reach TSL start.

The issue with the former is that you might miss the lock-in point; the issue with the latter is that you are likely to get stopped out for the LockInProfit.

I do have 'standard' BE code in the EA that is currently commented out.  It consists of two parameters:

BE_At

BE_Profit

The way the standard code works is:
If BE_At is not zero, then the SL will be moved to BE when the number of pips profit is reached.If BE_Profit is not zero, then the SL will be moved past BE to lock in the number of pips profit.Trailing SL works only when price is ahead of either the OpenPrice or the SL (whichever is greater) by the specified trailing value.

This would cater for both scenarios mentioned:

TrailStart=23

TrailStep=2

BE_At=33

BE_Profit=10

and

TrailStart=35

TrailStep=5

BE_At=35

BE_Profit=30

The only issue I have with this is that it is introducing ever more variations to test out, but could possibly help in those 'bad' periods...

--- 帖子 #1663 ---
Oh, so when you said 'trail as normal' you meant trail from OpenPrice and not the SL.

In my previous example, this would be achieved by:

TrailStart=15

TrailStep=2

BE_At=23

BE_Profit=10

--- 帖子 #1669 ---
Basically, what you're describing is a 15/2 trailing stop, i.e. you start trailing after the SL is moved into profit by 10 pips, but you then start trailing the stop in steps of 2 with a distance of 15 (25-10=15).

So, we're talking the same strategy, but the parameters would be set as I'd described.

It may make a bit more sense if I reverse the order of the parameters like this:

BE_At=23

BE_Profit=10

TrailStart=15

TrailStep=2

So: when price is 23 pips in profit, SL is moved to +10 pips, and then price trails by 15 pips in steps of 2.

--- 帖子 #1685 ---
UK Moves to DST

As the UK has moved their clocks forward this weekend, the London open now begins at 09:00 GMT.

The default trading times for ULTRON_PDV is 07:00-19:00 GMT (basically the most volatile period of the London and New York sessions), so these need to be moved forward 1 hour to compensate.

This is done, by subtracting 1 from the Broker Offset, so my setting (currently at +3) will revert to +2.

I urge you all to do the same, but the choice is yours, of course.

--- 帖子 #1702 ---
ULTRON_PDV_106

Updates:Corrected colour of figures on info panel. Added trend details to info panel (everything has to be green for a trade to open). Added a separate MA setting for the Retrace Exit figure (currently defaulted to 50 - the same as MA3). Added break-even settings and logic.

The break even logic is checked before the trailing stop logic, and the trailing stop only starts when the price is in profit by BreakEventAt+TrailinsgtopStart pips.

Setting BreakEvenAt to zero (the default) turns off the break even logic.

--- 帖子 #1807 ---
Guys Ultron is made for GBPUSD H1 only. And you Guys are spoiling my plans to test Ultron on basket 28+Gold pairs H1 starting from next week with tight SL 10pips instead 50/70/100 pips..  (Less than H1 will increase number of losing trades therefore I disagree with less than H1 until & unless you make TIGHT SL for 1minute chart to 1pip, 5minutes to 2.5pips, 5pips to 15minutes chart, and 7.5pips to 30minutes chart).

Anyways:

1- Special Thanks to PAWEL for sharing his EA with us.

2- Thanks FEEX to initiate / beautify Ultron and include trailing-SL.

3- Thanks MRDFX to give his feedback to ultron, at one point mrdfx said to leave original version on its own and don't change. I agreed with him and been live with Pawel version until recently changed to Paul version with trailing-sl.

4- Thanks Paul & cdsaa joined this Ultron together.

My testing conclusion::::

1- Pawel's version is 50pips bet each trade, it hits either 50pips profit or 50pips loss FIXED. If you make 50pips Loss so next trade can recover 50pips. winning rates 58% .

2- Feex & Paul versions are trailing-sl that's how trade close in profit for 3pips, 9pips, 13pips, and sometimes 43pips Not fixed. Winning rate is between 90% to 95%.

However, 1 losing trade gives you -70pips dent, eat up most of profit.

This is VOLUME EA, ENTRY is perfect in GREEN zone and profit secure by trailing-sl. Sounds good & PERFECT ENTRY .

Some trade does not trigger trailing-sl therefore trade goes to RED ZONE and can either retrace to GREEN ZONE or close with 50pips, 70pips, 100pips loss OUUCHHHH .

This is up to Pawel, feex, mrdfx, cdsaa, and Paul to discuss how to deal with losing TRADE with 50pips, 70pips, and 100pips dent/loss.

--- 帖子 #1814 ---
For some of the newer members in this thread:

Pawel's original EA as well as all other versions were designed to run specifically in the H1 time-frame on the GBP/USD pair. The parameters for entry were developed from analysis of that specific pair on that specific time-frame. While experimentation is always encouraged, it's likely the values of every single parameter the EA uses to determine when to open a position would have to change drastically in order to be profitable on anything other than the GBP/USD pair, if it could be profitable at all. This is not a universal EA. This was and always will be a very specific EA for a very specific pair and time-frame. Just something to keep in mind for everyone attempting to run the EA on other pairs.

--- 帖子 #1826 ---
They all use the same entry criteria.

OP has the values hard-coded, so you need to amend the source to make changes to them.

LITE has the variables externalised so you can amend them at will, and also allows for trailing stop and money management.

PDV is almost the same as LITE except it has additional trade management and money management functions,

There are several members here running all three versions with slightly differeing results due to differences in SL/TP, etc., so it's really a case of using whichever you feel most comfortable with really.

--- 帖子 #1848 ---
Adding to losing positions "just in case" is a really bad idea in my opinion.

If I understand you correctly, we add to a losing position in the hope that it turns around and wins.  If it wins, then it wins 2.5 times the original reward, but if it loses, it loses 1.5 time the original risk.

It's not something I feel would work, personally.

--- 帖子 #1849 ---
Yes it's more risky, but I mean when second trade add it start calculate profit from second trade, and it need just half the way to first trade opened to BE, and we can use that option just as rescue on retrace if we want to, and we can trail profit also. That was just an idea, I don't say it must be good, but maybe worth to test.

It's better to cut your losses than add to it. It's a terrible thing to hope for the markets to turn in one's favour considering we have no control over market forces. That's why personally I'm beginning to detest Scalping systems with huge SL.

Best you can do is stack the odds in your favour and let market forces determine the outcome. Personally I favour small SL and big TP. That way even a few number of losses won't eat up all the profits you've made with one trade hitting TP. The present settings with Ultron has proven beyond reasonable doubts to be a winner and I'm convinced that even without the trailing feature - which is of course a great addition in my opinion - Ultron will still be a long term winner with TP of 100 and SL of 70 as per the default.

You can't win them all. I know we traders don't like to see red in our accounts but like George Soros said (and I paraphrase) "It's not about how many wins or losses you have but how much you win when you win and how much you lose when you lose"

--- 帖子 #1877 ---
It doesnt matter whether this trade or any particular 1 trade wins or looses - whats important is the statistical edge which means it should win more than it looses over time.

One thing we can learn from the current buy order is that this EA is able to open an order into resistance or support or into a spike as the momentum builds. This leads us to perhaps adding some code to prevent this type of entry - easier said than done i know. However some early ideas could be;

1. using a market profile indicator for x period of time prior to the current time, to filter out entries where the price is approaching a price where the price has spent a very brief amount of time (only prior spikes) in the previous x period of time above (or below if short) the proposed entry price. Once this value = zero then the price has obviously broken through the level where it has not spent any time (above or below spikes during previous x period) and then entry is allowed. This is logic is designed to filter out entries where there have been previous spikes but allow them once the price has broken new ground... the tuning of x period in the market profile indi would be needed but easy enough to do with backtest. A suffiently large number would also = trade allowed if the price had spent a long time (or large volume) in the previous range of x period in the market profile.

2. using ADR to filter out entries if the price is near extreme level of ADR - entries near ADR 100% or above perhaps have a high likelyhood of reversal?

3. Filter out entries that occur within x pips of daily or weekly pivot points imported via dll data site - again to avoid entry close to likely reversal points

4. Filter out trades if RSI is above or below 70/30 @ period (input variable) also to tune via backtesting. long > 70 and short < 30 not allowed etc

Thats all i have for now, apologies if any of this has been tried before

--- 帖子 #1940 ---
guys - if you keep messing with the orders and changing things you will not reproduce the profitable edge that the back testing shows. You have to let the trades run to completion and accept the losses when they occur - you dont know which trades will end in profit and which fail - nobody can know, nobody ever knows when they place any forex trade...

As to the current short position - yes it looks like it opens at support again. However this support could also break lower and if it does we will have a profitable trade. My position is in DD and still running...

I also back tested at 99.9% alpari pro ECN data in TDS last 12 months the different settings with TP =  35 and SL = 70. Both with and without trailing stop, and breakeven pips settings etc. None of them produced more profitble result that PDV106 default setting. Some were close - but still none were better over the last year.

For those of you backtesting over a short period of time or with the std data in Mt4 without TDS - your simply wasting your time. You will not accurately model what the EA would have done. The biggest problem is the lack of variable spread in the back test. So when liquidity drops during NY to Asia time - the spreads can get huge and your back test will think it can close an order at a price that is not realistic when the spread is factored. This can skew your results significantly and make them look far different to what it really should have been...

--- 帖子 #1958 ---
One thing I learnt these last cpl of weeks was to just leave the EA alone to do its job, and trust in the strategy.

Manually intervening with some of the orders has backfired and I incurred a bigger loss than I should have. By increasing the SL "hoping" that GU will turn up meant incurring a larger loss when the extended SL was hit early this morning while I was still sleeping. If I had left the original SL intact I would have taken a smaller loss.

Another thing that had me too involved was the lot size of the trade. My risk % was set too high so the order was carrying an unnecessary high risk. Yeah it would be a good thing if the trade would have hit TP, but not so good when it hits SL.

I've now lowered the risk %, so form now on smaller orders but a lot safer. It might take longer to make those nice high profits we had in the back tests but at least I won't feel nervous about any orders.

Just gotta remind myself that forex is a journey not a race.

--- 帖子 #1968 ---
Could we consider using the RSI then?

The last 2 buys which ended in a loss opened at RSI 70 and above which indicates Ultron was buying at overbought level (no surprise there as those were major resistance zones). At such levels one should expect a reversal - at least in the short term even if the trend eventually continues upwards.

So we could say only Buy when RSI is 65 or lower (or 50 to 65) and only Sell when RSI is 35 or higher (or 50 to 35) after all other conditions have been met.

At least at 65 we know there's still a little room at the top so buyers can still push price higher so if they tend to be a reversal around the 70 RSI then the TS should protect the trade as such move from 65 to 70 should produce about 23 pips or more. However, if price moves over the 70 and a bit higher we just might get to as much as about 70pips. The Buy order of April 2, 2019 at 1.3098 illustrates that with price reaching about 80pips before the reversal, though that was even a key resistance level. Same logic applies to the 35 level for Sell trades. For sell instance see the Sell order of March 28, 2019 at 1.3151; also that was opened at a key support level.

Just my own brain'storming'

--- 帖子 #1971 ---
I've already tried adding in RSI and Stochastics, but they absolutely ruined the results.  The problem is that you end up throwing away more winning trades than losing trades.

The thing about this EA and its entry method is that it will almost always be trading into an overbought/oversold position, because it's following a trend and jumping in once the trend has already been established, which usually means getting in at the height of the move.  It then waits out the inevitable pull back in the hope of a continuation.

I've even looked at bollinger bands, but again, it trades into positions where conventional wisdom says you avoid when trading bollinger bands.

I'm happy to entertain any other ideas that people have though.

--- 帖子 #1973 ---
Hi Paul, i made these suggestions earlier in the thread but perhaps you missed them? Some ideas are;

1. using a market profile indicator like TPO or similar (i can attach it if your not familiar with it) for x period of time prior to the current time, to filter out entries where the price is approaching a price where the price has spent a very brief amount of time (prior spikes can be measured by volume and period comparison) in the previous x period of time (lookback time). Once this value = zero in the lookback period, then the price has obviously broken out of the current range where it has not spent any time (above or below spikes during previous x period) and then entry is allowed. This is logic is designed to filter out entries where there have been previous spike tops/bottoms but allow them once the price has broken new ground above or below this support/resistance. The challenge is to define an appropriate lookback period which is not too long, so that not too many entries are filtered out.

2. Another idea is using ADR (average daily range to filter out entries if the price is near 100% level of ADR - entries near ADR 100% perhaps have a high likelyhood of reversal. Again once the price breaks well above 100% ADR - the trade should be allowed again as strong trends begin with smashing through 100% ADR and often continue on to 200% or more...

3. Not sure how difficult it would be - but perhaps as a start we could even manually define levels which prevent a buy or sell opening within x pips of the manually defined price - simply consult the chart and look left at the previous spikes and define a level based on what can be seen by the user. Again once the price breaks well through that level - then allow the trade once again... Cannot be back tested is a problem with this tho...

just throwing ideas out there...

--- 帖子 #1980 ---
The real issue with applying filter after filter is that even if the filters remove the losses you are using them for, they will also remove wins - there's an averaging out effect which is almost impossible to get around.

The upshot is that, while you may smooth out the equity curve, you will almost certainly reduce the profitability of the EA itself.

I've also tried ATR to avoid trades where there's less 'room' in the day's movement than has been the average for the past few days, but that too has resulted in a massive reduction in profitability.

Personally, I'm coming to the conclusion that we've take this EA as far as we can, and have to accept the losses that it incurs as being part of the overall strategy.

I will continue to 'tinker' in the background with small changes such as different trailing stop strategies and variable targets, etc., and will post something new if I find something that seems to make a notable difference.

--- 帖子 #1981 ---
Try amending MA Period 3 from 50 to 48 (and, if you use the Retrace Exit, the Retrace Exit MA from 50 to 48).

You should see an improvement of roughly 10% in profitability.

--- 帖子 #1984 ---
I think "we" just might be approaching this EA the wrong way. This EA is designed to catch the start of a trend for the GBPUSD which means in a sideways or erratic market with very unusual volatility it will fail - No offence here. Of course we all know the state of the GBPUSD presently.

Now, what if instead of trying to modify the EA we turn to a pair with similar behaviour as the GBPUSD only this time this correlated pair isn't affected by the level of volatility GBPUSD is facing. I wrote about the GBPJPY and heard it did poorly in backtest. Honestly, while I don't undermine the necessity of backtest, like someone said: we are meant to trade the futures not history. Backtesting gives you a clue of a strategy's performance but forward testing tells you if it works in the present market conditions, as we know that the market is dynamic and changes very often.

That said, I've been demo testing quite a number of correlated pairs to the GBPUSD and have found the GBPJPY, EURUSD, GBPAUD doing what GBPUSD was designed to do - I mean doing great. I've looked at how the trades are opened in line with price action and the logic is sound. I'm yet to have a losing trade on those pairs and between them I've had about 8 trades (started testing from March 20, 2019). I have them set for 40 or 50pips TP1 and 80 or 100pips TP2 - depending on the pair - using another EA called Trade Manager to manage the TP levels. Presently I still have a EURUSD trade that just got to TP1 so I'm on a risk free ride at the moment and a GBPJPY that has hit TP2.

What I'm trying to say here in a nutshell is that we shouldn't try to force Ultron to adapt to every market changes as it won't. It's a robot not a human. But we can identify market price action and then decide whether to use Ultron with a different pair from what it's designed for or turn it off completely until the market corrects itself again. Personally I plan on studying the EA more and then utilize some price action skill to know when to turn it on or off and which pair to use it with when I do turn it on but those pairs have to be correlated with the GBPUSD since it's the pair the author designed it with. He definitely had quite a bunch in his mind when he opted for GBPUSD for the strategy and I have to respect that. I've had Ultron turned off for the GBPUSD after my last loss on the 12th of April wherein I did a lil rant on the forum - my apologies if I offended a few. So I guess I was lucky to avoid the recent loss(es).

So think on it people. It's just my 2 cents here.

More Greens

EDIT: The simple way to know that Ultron isn't doing great with GBPUSD is seeing it open Buys at Resistance and Sells at Support and that the pair is swinging up and down in a sideways move. Yes a few breakouts - both real and false - but it then returns to the same range again repeating the same pattern; a real red flag if you ask me.

--- 帖子 #1985 ---
I was haunted by the option of TP 35)
In the version ULTRON_LITE_3.7 now there are two options for trailing stop.
In the default settings, the first option works, to which we are all accustomed.
The second option "Tralling_from_Profit" works differently: the trailing works after the price reaches the TP level.
If "Tralling_from_Profit" is TRUE, then set Trailing Stop 4, Trailing Step 2. TP 35
The picture is a rough test of this option. Work time I used 10 and 23 (GMT+3 broker)
You can change at your convenience.
If someone can test this option with a simulation quality of 99.9%, then it will be more clear if this makes sense or not.
P.S.
I used 1:300 leverage. It is interesting to look at the result with a leverage of 1:500

You can do the same test (same period) with these settings:
TP=38
SL=70
OpenHour=10
CloseHour=23
Trailing=true
Tralling_from_Profit=true
Risk Ratio=10
TrailingStop=4
TrailingStep=2
ExponentialFactorDecrease=0.5

and
TP=38
SL=70
OpenHour=8
CloseHour=23
Trailing=true
Tralling_from_Profit=true
Risk Ratio=10
TrailingStop=4
TrailingStep=2
ExponentialFactorDecrease=0.5

Thank you very much for your tests. I was interested to see the difference between TP35 and TP38, as well as starting time 8 and 10. I noticed a strange thing: ICMarkets shows the best results from TP35 and start time 8, while ROBOFOREX shows the best results from TP38 and start time 10. If I understand correctly, both brokers work as GMT + 3. The difference in leverage - ICMarkets 1: 500, ROBOFOREX 1: 300.

And I cannot understand why TP35 is better on one broker, TP38 on another is better. Starting time is 8 on one better, on the other 10 better ....

As for reducing the ratio - I noticed that there is no difference between 1 and 0.5, I just wanted to make sure that it does not depend on the broker. With a decrease in the coefficient of 0.8 and 0.7, my results were worse than even with a factor of 0.9

--- 帖子 #2123 ---
Three red dots appear if the transaction is open and is currently negative. If there are no open trades, the three dots will always be yellow. If you have something wrong, make a screenshot of the entire trading schedule with an information panel.

--- 帖子 #2149 ---
Little is not clear your disappointment. No adviser will profit from forever. This is an axiom. No great tests for a long period do not give any guarantees that tomorrow this system will work the same way. This must be understood initially, if you come to the market. For profitable work of any adviser, certain market conditions are needed, and since the market is constantly changing, the conditions for the use of this or that adviser will also change, which naturally affects your profit.

The ULTRON system is a working system that brings profit under certain conditions. If market conditions are suitable for this system - it brings profit. If not - then you get a loss. That's how all systems work.

--- 帖子 #2190 ---
Thanks, that was helpful.

Looking through the data, you have different time filters, which could cause differences in the number of trades opened.  You also have the Volume parameter set differently, which again will cause one EA to skip a trade where the other doesn't.

The only difference in trades was a losing trade opened by 106 on 12.07.2019 - 105 didn't open a trade at this time.  Looking at the time it was opened (5pm local time) I suspect that it was the Volume that caused 105 to skip the trade but 106 to open it.

All other trades appeared to open and close together, which is what I wold have expected.

The other main difference is in the lot sizes.  For 105 you're risking 25% of the available equity, but in 106 you're risking only 1% of the account balance.  This will yield wildly different results percentage-wise, for the same trades.

So, to sum up, I'm happy that 106 is doing what it should and it's just the settings that have made the difference here.

Hi arci11,

That is how I use the Ultron system, correct. It initially was a bit of an experiment over the months that Ultron was evolved thru several versions. I use Exponential 3.3 on GBP/EUR and on EUR/USD..... and Ultron Lite 3.7 on GBP/AUD and also on GBP/CAD.

I turn off all the above Ultron pairs and I don't personally trade on Monday and on Friday due to my own method of trading the Forex market for certain reasons. Overall, I do not fully depend on Ultron. Sometimes I see that the system opens a trade right at a support or resistance level and I analysis whether I should stay in the trade or not, based on the direction it opened versus the support or resistance levels. Sometimes I close the trade with a small gain or loss. Hours later, I'm proven that I did the right move. Analyzing Support and Resistance levels are key in Forex trading.

Hope that helps arci11

--- 帖子 #2273 ---
hi , can i ask if possible (in future versions) SL ,TP and trailing SL can be also dynamic using ATR

enable ATR = yes (will ignore the static SL,TP and trailing SL)

ATR period =14

dynamic SL = 1.5 (1.5 x current ATR with period 14)

dynamic TP = 2

dynamic Traili SL = 1

etc

i check the atr just few min ago and for GBPUSD 1h = 40

so

if a trade opened the dynamic SL ,TP and trailing SL will be

ATR period =14

dynamic SL = 1.5 (1.5 x 40 = 60 pips)

dynamic TP = 80 pips

etc

and of course a lot of back testing will needed .. (the above config is only an example)

dynamic Traili SL = 40 pips

Also a good idea also is having 2 position open

i mean if fixed lot = 0.10 (open 2 positions with 0.05)

if risk percentage is 1.0% (open 2 position win 0.5% each)

also will need in config Sl1, Sl2,TP1, TP2 and also the same with dynamic SL and TP

example

SL 1 position = 70 pips

Sl 2 position = 70 pips

TP 1 position = 50 pips

TP2 position =150

..

Dynamic SL 1 = 1.5 (i give the example above)

Dynamic SL 2 = 1.5

Dynamic Tp 1 = 1

Dynamic TP 2 = 5

Trailing SL = 1

..

with this can lock half profits soon and a lot of later on as the trend can be very big some times

and of course the above numbers is an example only a lot of backtesting will needed of optimum config ...

--- 帖子 #2314 ---
I have written an implementation of the Ultron robot for the cTrader platform.

To know more about cTrader see:
http://ctrader.com
http://help.ctrader.com

The robot uses GMT times, and automatically takes into account the shift of one hour in the summer months (daylight saving time). That is, the allowed trading hours are shifted one hour earlier in summer.

The robot is profitable in my backtest between January 2014 and September 2020. The backtest has been done with high quality tick data, starting capital 10000 EUR and fixed lot size 0.01.

The source code is available. If you know how to program for cTrader and you manage to make this robot more profitable please let us know.

Before you ask questions about the robot, make sure that you have read and understood this whole thread in the forum and the manual of the robot.

--- 帖子 #2325 ---
Hi everyone,

I've read through alot of the thread and would like to try Ultron Lite, and with a trailing stop like I think FEEX used/uses.

However I'm struggling to see what his exact settings/times are?

He said the following during the thread, but I'm not sure if they are upto date? Also it doesn't mention about stop loss.

I was haunted by the option of TP 35)

In the version ULTRON_LITE_3.7 now there are two options for trailing stop.

In the default settings, the first option works, to which we are all accustomed.

The second option "Tralling_from_Profit" works differently: the trailing works after the price reaches the TP level.

If "Tralling_from_Profit" is TRUE, then set Trailing Stop 4, Trailing Step 2. TP 35

The picture is a rough test of this option. Work time I used 10 and 23 (GMT+3 broker)

You can change at your convenience.

If someone can test this option with a simulation quality of 99.9%, then it will be more clear if this makes sense or not.

P.S.

I used 1:300 leverage. It is interesting to look at the result with a leverage of 1:500

Thanks!

--- 帖子 #2327 ---
Very good! So you mean you actually modified the v1.2 code, so that's what this v1.3 is?

They are good results for 6 years, and acceptable drawdawn too.... One concern is that the gross loss is huge, like 80% of the gross profit,, does it mean it's mainly fees eating into the profit?

Also what reason did you choose to modify 1.2 rather than another version?

Thanks!!

--- 帖子 #2328 ---
Yes, I modified the v1.2 code and named it v1.3.

The gross loss comes from the losing trades. There are no fees involved. The gross loss from the original version is ~75%. So there is no big difference. Version 1.3 takes bigger risk in favor of bigger profit. So you will have a bigger gross loss, but also bigger net profit.

I've chosen the v1.2 because it looked the best to me. All the other versions in this thread performed badly or didn't show any significant improvement.

Original ULTRON v1.2:
Attached Image (click to enlarge)

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

--- 帖子 #2330 ---
I like the simplicity of Ultron. To be able to better backtest its performance, I ported the v1.2 source code to MT5. I have seen some other MT5 ports before in this thread, but no one posted the source code. So for those interested, I have attached the port from MT4 to MT5 of the original ULTRON v1.2 code of post #6 without any modifications.
Attached File(s)   ULTRON1.2.mq5

4 KB
|
485 downloads

Unfortunately, it looks like the days for Ultron are over. It was probably heavily optimized at the time of release. You might want to try to re-optimize for today's conditions, but beware that there are many hardcoded values in the source code that you would first need to turn into an input parameter for MT5 to optimize.

--- 帖子 #2333 ---
Good that you double check the result! However, please make sure you run a reliable backtest. Judging from your screenshot, it appears you used MT4 to backtest and only used Open Prices. That is not a representative backtest.

I recommend you test again using MT5 using *Real* ticks (not fake ticks). This will automatically download tick data from your broker, simulate slippage and requotes, etc. You will see that the results are completely different.
